<Author>isvaradeva
<Content>Wanna Be Luxury The reason why I know that this is a luxury hotel is because they tell me it is, but frankly few of the experiences here are luxury. First the good....1. The staff with relatively few exception is friendly (although the restaurant staff can be slow) and competent. Every time I returned to the hotel, the staff greeted me with a warm welcome and made me feel like I was coming home. 2. If you get a room with a view of the harbor, it is an awesome view. The Statue of Liberty is right outside the windows and it is nice to watch the boats pass by. 3. For a high end hotel, wi fi is relatively cheap ($12.95/night or $59.95 for seven nights). I will never understand why wi fi is free at a Motel 6 but not at a hotel for which you pay $500 a night but the Ritz is no different than other high end hotels. Since most in my experience charge $25/day (highway robbery), the Ritz price wasn't too bad.Now the bad. 1. The room itself is quite plain. For a hotel catering to business travelers it is amazing how few outlets there are to plug in computers etc. The toiletries are Bulgari, but they provide very few of them. 2. The room service menu is appallingly bad. There is very little to choose from in general and the choices are nowhere near the standards of most luxury hotels (dry rubbery hamburgers, pizza etc.) Frankly, the restaurant is not much better. While there are more choices of food, the fare is unimaginative and average. 3. The hotel lacks basics like a stocked sundry shop. I don't expect the a whole pharmacy but if I forget my deodorant, I find it preposterous that I can get a replacement at the Crown Plaza but not at the Ritz (actually they had Speed Stick for men, but nothing for women. Obviously in a pinch you wear what the have, but are women not business travelers too? Must I smell like a teenager going to prom in bad cologne?) . Nor can you get a magazine, a pack of gum or other basics. You can however, buy very expensive yuppie candles.I haven't stayed at other hotels downtown, but I will definitely look for other options the next time I must be in this area.  
<Date>Oct 28, 2008

<Author>Mahaguru
<Content>Peaceful NYC Alternative I enjoyed my 3-night stay but take it in light of the hotel location, 4 mins walk from my destination, and the fact that I had no time to enjoy NYC on this trip. The rooms are as comfortable as you'd expect but the big treat, I think, is having the unobstructed view of the harbour and enough quiet that you can open the window at night. Hotel services and food are good. This is a great place to stay for a change of pace in NYC - nice walking path along the river and a surprisingly mellow atmosphere in the Battery Park/Gateway Plaza neighborhood. The hotel is more than a walk from anywhere in Manhattan, Wall Street excepted, and you'd probably end up taking a taxi everywhere you need to go. The tradeoff for being more in the middle of things, entertainment-wise, is the view and relaxed neighborhood.

<Author>Francofinn
<Content>Nice hotel, but more 4-star than 5-star I got a nice offer on this hotel through BA Holidays website.Otherwise I wouldn't never have spent 500 $+tax per night for that hotel !First of all, let's speak about the view. Everybody seems to find it amazing... It's true they easily upgrade you to a harbour view room (so why spending 100 $ per night when you are very able to get the nice room for the price of a city view room...?), but I didn't find the view that extraordinary. Maybe for NYC it's, but you only see some grey water and the Statue of Liberty far away (that's very nice though, because you have a telescope in the room). The second fact is that the hotel isn't very tall (only 14 stories), so it's quite impossible to have a breathtaking view (personally I enjoy a lot being on a very high floor...).The room was very clean and big, the bed wonderful ! But when you look at the room you don't feel like being in a 5-star hotel. Furnishings are very average.Bathroom is really nice with WC, bathtub and shower apart. Nice Bulgari amenitites also.There is one thing I found quite strange : the quality of housekeeping changed every day... ! One day we had free bottles of water, one day we hadn't... One day we had three chocolates on the bed, one day we had only one... One day there were new bottles of conditioner, shampoo and lotion, one day we had to deal with the almost empty old ones...After all, the location is good and bad at the same time... If you want to be in a quiet and sterile area, it's probably the best hotel in NYC. But if you want to be near all, in the middle of the hectic NYC citylife, stay elsewhere. If you go Midtown and back, that will cost you around 30$ (15$ one way), plus tip... !

<Author>londoneagle
<Content>Perfect Location We have just returned from a 5 night stay at the Ritz Carlton Batt Park having visited New York 4 times before.We chose this hotel because of a special deal from British Airways and the good location.The hotel is based at the very end of Manhatton often referred to as Lower Manhatton or Downtown. It is right next to all the ferries and many hotel rooms have a magnificant view of the Statue of Liberty.It is also next to the city and all the skyscrapers, so the other hotel rooms also have an incredible view.You can easily walk to the WTC site, Wall street, South Seaport and there is an underground stop very closeby which gives you access to the rest of NY.The area is very safe and it was great visiting 5th Avenue and Times square via underground, but it was also great getting away from the madness to the tranquility of the Ritz Carlton.You get a real chance to experience the real New York as most of the restaurants and bars are full of locals - not tourists.Went to Bobby Vans, River Cafe, Bateaux Cruise, 2-West and One by Land Two by Sea. All fantastic, probably ranked in the order I listed them.Not cheap in this area except for clothes.Service in hotel very good and cocktail bar on 14th floor has outdoor spectacular views of Statue Liberty. We thought we were mixing with Sex in the City types and we couldnt resist joining in by ordering cosmopolitans as in the film.

<Author>HLana
<Content>Not worth the money I completely agree with the previous review by dannymcl--pretentious, overstaffed, high-class chain. The beds were very comfortable, but the room was dusty--very dusty in corners. Housekeeping was below average. We had to remake the beds to fix the problem with the mattress pads. The worst part was the breakfast at the hotel restaurant. The omlet consisted of a big lump of egg with just a few pieces of veges and ham inside--extremely unappetizing. What was supposed to be hashbrowns was a deep-fried lump of potato shreds. I ordered French Toast which seemed also deep fried. The breakfast for my family (two adults and two kids) cost 95 dollars, and it wasn't worth it!!! The wait staff looked so tired and unhappy at 9:00 am. If you want a good breakfast, go to the cafe near the hotel. The name starts with a Z and it's just a block away. The following few days, we stayed at Hotel Commonwealth in Boston--first class experience. Next time, we will reconsider staying at the ritz; instead, I am going to try another boutique hotel like Hotel Commonwealth. Other small lluxury hotels are listed on the website--www.slh.com.

<Author>Jay175
<Content>Hmmm mixt feelings Stayed in the hotel end of July with my wife and two teenage daughters.First of all great location, we came to NY to relax and this is the palce to be... It's out of the hussle of mid town, but realy not that far away.The staff were very good, however, almost over the top... we started to feel they were being over polite to get tips (front door..)But it's perhaps not the case, as everything went very well. Taxies were very easy to get.The check in was fast even though we were early... however no up-grades as the hotel was full due to a wedding.The rooms are quite a good size for NY, great view of the statue, however, the rooms do need a make over as the are well worn and at these prices it's not realy acceptable. a flat screen tv would help. This is not a 5 star hotel, and I think it's not right to rely on service to cover up the outdated property.

<Author>PerthiteOZ
<Content>Best decision was to stay here Whilst some may like noise and crowds, we do not. Having stayed in NYC twice before, this time we chose the Ritz Battery Park because of its location in a less popular tourist area. And we got it 100% right! The staff were attentive without being over the top. The room was very well appointed and a lovely size, including the bathroom. We had a City View Club room - did not want or ask for a Harbour view as my husband wished to photograph the buildings at night from our window. We were lucky enough to be able to see both the river and the buildings from our window so no complaints from him. The bed was exceptionally comfortable. We had room service one night and whilst expensive, was prompt and edible without being outstanding. The Restaurant was ok -I found the servers to be a bit snobbish and also a little supercilious in their approach to me as opposed to my husband.The Club Lounge was brilliant - except when there were noisy children there which I felt should have been kept quiet by their parents - after all, it is not a play room. Perhaps the Club Concierge would have spoken to the adults if we had asked but we preferred to return to our room with our drinks rather than upset anyone. Our choice. This did not spoil our view of the Club Lounge - the breakfast choices, lunch a la carte and late night nibblies plus free wi fi were all a hit with us. The Club Concierge also sorted out a billing error we had. We placed our own water in our mini bar fridge which required moving items already in there around (but not out of) the fridge. We were charged over $100 for items that were still in the fridge - purely because apparently the person who replenishes the bar just opens it, looks to where items are supposed to be and bills accordingly. Not a good system and one which could have proven quite expensive for us. But the amounts were reversed without fuss.The location is excellent for the subway - we journeyed up town a few times with ease. We also walked to Soho and Little Italy and if you are going to go to Century 21, it is a short walk away - very convenient for their early openings. One night we dined in the Meat Packing District, a $15 cab fare.The ability to walk through the Battery Park gardens and along the river early in the mornings with little noise or fuss was very cathartic. We will definitely stay again.

<Author>denrusso
<Content>Great Hotel with Superb Service I booked a city view club level room here during Columbus Day weekend for a little RR with the wife. Service was spot on as soon as we arrived. Door men were attentive with plenty of bell hops to care for your luggage. Upon entering the lobby I asked if I could be escorted to the club lounge where I could check-in (club level room key required for the elevator to stop at the appropriate floor). At the 'club' my wife and two of my guests (they were not staying, only visiting momentarily) were allowed to sit and enjoy one of their food presentations (not charged extra for my guests). One of the best 'check-in' experiences I have gone through. I even ask for, and was given, and upgrade to a Harbor view room. It was also during this time that I started talking with the concierge for restaurant recommendations. He had numerous French restaurants within walking distance fax their menus for my review. My wife and I decided to take a stroll around Battery Park and through the financial district before making a decision. Once we returned, on a whim, I asked if Per Se was available - to our surprise, the concierge was able to secure us a reservation for two (by all means, no easy task).We did not eat at any of the restaurants at the hotel and hence cannot comment on them. The room was clean and well appointed. The telescope was more decoration then anything else. With a Ritz Carlton, you're paying a premium for top-notch attentive service and their Battery Park location does not disappoint...

<Author>citygirl4616
<Content>Nice retreat from the hustle and bustle of midtown I stayed at this Ritz for 3 nights with my husband for my 40th birthday celebration. I come to NY several times a year, and we always stay in midtown or uptown. I decided for a change of scenery, we would try the Ritz at Battery Park. It is a lovely location, right on the waterfront. The evenings were quiet, and perfect for a relaxing stroll after dinner. We had a Harbor view room overlooking the Statue of Liberty, which was very special. The hotel is beautiful...definitely up to the Ritz standards. Service was always helpful and friendly, and there was nothing the staff wouldn't do to accomodate us. This is the Ritz though, and everything is pricey. It was painful to pay $350 for a 1 hour couples massage, although the spa was nice, and the massage was excellent. Breakfast in bed was $90 (1 order of waffles and an order of poached eggs). Dinner in the dining room downstairs was $185 for 2. Unless it is a special occasion, or you are on an expense account, the prices really sting. My weekend was a splurge, so I tried not to let it bother me.Battery Park is located right near the financial district. It is not the most exciting part of town. I was looking for a quiet, relaxing weekend, and I got it. The downside is, we had to take the subway, or a cab everywhere. There is not much in Battery Park to do. My favorite restaurants, shopping and museums are all uptown. Even the Village and Soho are not really walking distance. That will probably affect my decision whether to stay there again or not. I like being able to walk outside my hotel, and having everything right outside my door.The room was very nice and the bed was incredibly comfortable. The bathroom was very large for a NYC hotel room. Housekeeping and room service were friendly, professional, quick and efficient. The conceirge was always right on target with directions and recommendations, and the front desk staff was top notch.

<Author>gascony
<Content>Good business hotel downtown Haved stayed here 4 times this year (2008). Hotel is typical business hotel in a business district - would advise against staying here for vacation as there really is nothing but offices and a few basic coffee shop/cafes in the immediately area (although obviously has a fab view of the statue of liberty). Overall it's a high quality business hotel vs the conference type hotels you get so much in NY. Rooms are a decent size which is unusual in NY as are the bathrooms which come with good toiletries. Front desk service is always excellent. Laundry/housekeeping is a disaster - on 3 of the 4 trips they lost my pressing (!). Have only had a drink in the bar - would say it's average. Room service ok with limited choice. Breakfast is better from one of the nearby cafes. Given its location taxi's can be a nightmare - if you are going somewhere make sure you allow plenty of time for them to get you a taxi. this situation has improved a bit over the past few years but unlike the midtown or uptown hotels there is a lower level of available taxis. 5 minute walk to wall street etc which accounts for most of the guests.

<Author>BestYet
<Content>Big Disappointment!!! We stayed at the Ritz-Carlton Battery Park for six nights during the week before Easter. We had a suite because we brought our nine year old granddaughter for her first trip to New York (she lives in Austin, Texas). We paid quite a bit for the room, not out of line for a five star hotel in New York, but we were very disappointed with the inconsistency of service, the maintenance and the other aspects of the stay. On the one hand, sometimes the staff were friendly and helpful but many times they were not and ignored us (at times we felt as if we were strangers wandering through the lobby). Some examples: when we checked in we were told our bags would be brought to our room immediately. After waiting an half hour, I went to the lobby and our bags were still there. We had a similar experience on check out. I asked that our bags be taken down to lobby at a specific time when our ride to the airport was to arrive. No one came to our room at the appointed time and again I had to call. During our stay we found that the door to our room would not lock unless it was pulled tight to the frame. Normally it would have shut and locked on its own. We didn't discover this until coming back to our room after being out and finding it unlocked. When I called for repair no one came for a long time and when someone did come they really didn't do any thing to remedy the situation, The restaurant food was good but the service was very slow. The maid service was okay but inconsistent with turndown being done some nights and not others. There were other incidents but I have gone on too long. My greatest problem with this hotel is that it didn't live up to the standards that I expect from hotels of the caliber that Ritz-Carlton purports to be. I have traveled extensively throughout the world in a 30+ year career in international law and on pleasure trips with my wife. We have stayed at many grand hotels in London, Paris, Hong Kong (a Ritz-Carlton, Jakarta, Bali and many other places. The service I received at those hotels was far and above the level of service we received at the Ritz-Carlton Battery Park. As a matter of fact, just a month earlier we had stayed at the Fairmont Newport Beach and the experience was in sharp contrast starting with the valet taking our car as we arrived knowing my name having our bags brought to our room immediately. If we had stayed at a lesser hotel in New York I would not have found our experience disappointing since I would not have expected the level of service we should have received at the Ritz-Carlton. To compound the disappointment, after the stay we were called by the Ritz-Carlton chain to give a critique. Needless to say, I was quite negative and when I was asked if I would like to have someone from the hotel call, I said I did. A few days later I was called by a manager at the hotel named Prince Sanders. When I explained my problems he was highly apologetic and said he would follow up with the staff to make corrections. He also said he would send me a voucher for a night's stay at the hotel. That was a month and a half ago and I have received nothing.  
<Date>May 9, 2008

<Author>fcrouch
<Content>great stay at the battery park ritz we stayed 3 nights at the battery park ritz - club floor - harbor view room (had booked a city view but was upgraded - the hotel was not terribly busy). We had requested a room near the club lounge and that was also accomodated. We love Ritz club floors and this was no different - as it is a smaller hotel than some RC the club level staff would bring drinks rather than you fixing one yourself (though wine was available on as self service basis some of the time). we arrived mid-day and our room was available (we'd asked for early check-in) and again, because the hotel wasn't too busy- requested and received a late check-out on Monday. The location is great for lower Manhattan and also steps away from the number 4 subway line (lex av. express) - which has stops at Grand Central station, 86th street (a 5 minute walk to the met museum of art) and 59th street - for Central Park and shopping along 5th avenue). We enjoyed the quiet of the battery park area in the evening - we spent the evenings in the club lounge - our daughter made friends with some other kids staying on the club floor - so we hung out with the other parents in the lounge. Rooms quite nice (I think a little smaller than some R/C) but new - so there is a separate bath and shower. Small but nice gym with a great view. We did some in-room dining - typical but good. Would absolutely stay here again when visiting New York.

<Author>jc9276
<Content>A nice change of pace A group of friends and I who travel to New York annually to reunite, relax, and see a show or two decided to forego our usual digs in MIdtown/Time Square and camp out at the Ritz Carlton Battery Park. We booked club level rooms (only one of our rooms got upgraded to bay view after the first night) through American Express Platinum Travel. We were very pleased with the service, food presentations, and accomodations on that floor. Yes, there was the carpet stain here or there and no in-room coffee as discussed by previous reviewers, but all in all, compared to other crackerbox NYC rooms, this one was just fine. The view, once we were moved to a bayside view, was fantastic. The staff throughout the hotel were genuinely kind and greeted us at every chance possible. We also had two children (7 and 10) with us on this trip in one of the rooms, and at no time did the staff treat us differently. I had one issue with the front desk staff not handling our check-in correctly. I specifically called several days ahead and gave explicit instructions regarding not charging my friends who were to check in earlier than me (it was a birthday surprise). I was told that it would be taken care of and no problem in typical Ritz fashion. Although they completely flubbed this up, my stay from that point on was nice enough that I let it slide. The location is out of the way if you're new to the city and want to concentrate on the Midtown and Uptown touristy things. If you're not scared of trains and taxis to get up that way, I'd definitely recommend this Ritz Carlton. Oh, and ask for Raquel if you're on the club level. She was the epitomy of Ritz Carlton's commitment to service.

<Author>chonglh
<Content>Nice and quiet corner of the town We wanted to stay away from mid town but at the same time experience Manhattan. So, my husband and I booked Ritz in Battery PArk. My husband uses a wheelchair so it is important the the hotel room is reasonably spacious and accessible. For the price that we are paying, we are actually getting much more square foot. Many hotels did not understand that we need a roll-in shower, they will tell us that they have an accessible roll-in bath room but really all they have is a additional hand bar. And as I have expected from Ritz Carlton's standard, the Ritz hotel staff is well-trained and totally understood our needs and we did not have problems checking into the room we need for 2 nights.The lobby is very modern and understated, not your typical Ritz Carlton, it is more a business-trip hotel, or that's the feelings that I got. It didn't bother me since we are going out in town most of the time. We just want something that is comfortable and nice.The hotel is located at the southwestern tip of the city and offers a spectacular harbor views. There is absolutely nothing blocking your view and you can see the status of liberty right out your window. But you need to ask for a harbor view instead of city view, it will set you back $50 for that. Each room comes with a telescope but we couldn't get it to work. Parking is expensive, about $60 each day for Valet services. This hotel also has a very neighborhood feelings to it because it is surrounded by condos instead of hotels. You will see people walking the dogs, running, and the presence of police is everywhere. There are not many eateries near the hotel, you need to at least walk a few blocks and there is a grocery/convenient store that we loved. They serve really good hot breakfasts under $5 and $1 coffee that is awesome. They have snacks, deserts, pastries and hot sandwiches and sushi in a box. Awesome. There is also a new waterfront eatery which is beautiful at night and you can dine outside and watch the beautiful night scene.There is bus stop across the hotel so it is great. We took local bus to travel everywhere in town. In fact, that is the best way to explore Manhattan. Don't join the tour group which you pay like $70-80, because you can do the same thing by just spending a little more time reading the bus schedule and get to where you want as well. Since my husband uses a wheelchair, so public transportation is actually the best way to go, they are guaranteed accessible and it is so inexpensive.Overall, we feel that we are very happy with our rooms and the services are very good. It is quiet at night and away from the city buzz, if that's what you like, you will enjoy this hotel.

<Content>It was fine! We just got back from a 3 night stay at the Ritz Battery Park. We have previously stayed at the Four Seasons and Ritz Central Park. The hotel was fine, the staff were very friendly and the room was large and clean, my big thing is bathrooms and this was better than most. It is very out of the way and despite the harbor view my children decided that next time they'd rather stay in mid-town since that was where we spent most of our time anyway. When I'm staying at a Ritz Carlton I want it to feel like that and this one just didn't do it for us. All in all I have to say we would not stay here again with or without our children.

<Author>sambfh
<Content>Service with a smile This was our second stay at the RC Battery Park and was every bit as good as the first time, 4 years ago.The service is, in my opinion, what makes RC hotels stand out above the other upscale chains, like Mandarin Oriental  Four Seasons.We were greeted by name by reception as soon as we walked in ( a clever discreet microphone from the bellhop to reception ensures that they know who you are when you reach the desk) and offered lunch on the house (which we refused) when we were informed that we might have to wait an hour for our room...even though we were hours early for check in)The service remained friendly throughout our stay; requests were answered promptly, room service arrived quickly, always with a smile.We had booked a suite overlooking the harbour; it wasn't the biggest suite I have ever stayed in, nor the best equipped but it was the most comfortable bed and the room has stupendous views.If you are happy to spend time in Tribeca/Little Italy/Chinatown/Soho rather than uptown, you get the best views here and , IMHO, the best service.

<Author>trishg1972
<Content>Couldn't fault it We stayed here for four nights recently on a winter break to New York. I was a little apprehensive as we were travelling as a family with two children (aged 8  7) and I was not sure whether New York was a good travel choice. The flight was long (8 hours) because of the head wind and a little delayed but as soon as we got to the hotel, our moods improved. We were checked in quickly, got to the room (Harbour view) and were greeted with teddy bears for the kids, and a huge stack of cookies and milk! The room was fabulous, large with great toiletries (BVLGARI) and the service was just what I had hoped it would be for the Ritz Carlton. The staff throughout the hotel were fabulous and made a real fuss of the kids.We had breakfast in the restaurant each morning which was good - yes, it is expensive but that is what you expect in this sort of hotel. Service was fab - the waitress remembered our order each morning and never charged us for any of the kids food.We ate dinner one evening in 2 West and again, this was really good.One day there was lots of snow and the kids had a snowball fight outside the hotel. They walked back in absolutely covered in snow (despite our best efforts to wipe them down before they came indoors) , and dripping it all over reception. The reception staff simply came over, started having a snow ball fight with them indoors and offered them hot apple juice - this just summed up to me what a fantastic hotel it was.Only slight downer is the location. The views of the Statue of Liberty were amazing but it did mean a taxi ride if you wanted to go midtown - the weather was freezing cold with snow so even a walk to the subway seemed just too far!

<Author>MonkeysGirl
<Content>Perfect Stay We stayed one night on a layover in NYC. It was perfect. We flew in from out of the country on an excessively long flight. I had previously contacted the hotel about a romantic bath from their menu. My husband did not want to do it because we had dinner arrangements, and we were worried that our arriving flight would make us miss the beautiful bath. However, upon arriving at JFK on time, he remarked that he'd wished we had booked it. While he got our bags, I called the hotel under the premise that I was calling the car service. I spoke with Jason and explained quickly the situation. I asked if there were any Harbor View rooms since my husband, though very well traveled, had somehow never ended up in NYC and seen the Statue of Liberty. He was very helpful said it was not a problem to upgrade us or let us check in early. He then transferred me to a woman (whose name I can't remember because I have a horrid name memory), who listened to me very quickly recount that I wanted to have the romantic bath set up for our arrival in an hour. She said it usually took 24 hours to set it up because it involves fresh flowers. I said I understood, and would it be possible to set up something similar and skip the flowers? Right about that time, my husband was wheeling our luggage over, so I had to cut the conversation with an excessively curt, My husand is coming,and this is a surprise for him. Anything you can do would be great. Ok, bye. When we checked in they were preparing the room for our early check-in and handed us a glass of champagne while we waited in the lobby. When we walked in the room, my husband was so excited. I had not told him that the hotel upgraded us to the Harbor View room. The room was gorgeous and spacious. The telescope looking over the Statue of Liberty was truly unique and a lovely experience. I checked in the bathroom while my husband was otherwise occupied with the telescope and to my amazement, the staff had managed to set up the entire romantic bath, flowers and all!!! There were gorgeous mounds of bubbles strewn with rose petals, candles lining the tub, champagne chilling with delicious chocolates, a heart made of rose petals on the bathmat, and little containers of other bath amenities to add later on. It was truly spectacular. I finally got my husband away from the telescope long enough to look at the impressive display. He was so happy. I really could not believe they had managed the last minute request. It was such a surprise. The next morning, it was difficult to get out of such a comfortable bed. So, we ordered room service. It was quite good, and what we have come to expect from any Ritz dining experience. The hotel staff truly did outdo themselves. Thank you Ritz on making our very brief stay so pleasant!!

<Author>MrsFreshie
<Content>Everything First Class at the Ritz! We spent a lovely weekend at the Ritz at Battery Park, in part to celebrate my husband's birthday and also to attend a formal function. We booked a Harbor View room on the concierge level so that we could totally enjoy both the location and the hotel amenities. From the moment we arrived we were greeted by courteous and helpful staff that couldn鈥檛 do enough to please us. We weren鈥檛 totally satisfied with the first room we were given (too close to the elevator for my preference) and the staff went out of their way to accommodate us with a room more to our liking. Many thanks to Cullen for his persistence in finding a room that suited us! We found the concierge service absolutely lovely and well worth the extra money, the food presentations were tasty and plentiful, and the staff very happy to serve you in your room as well as in the lounge area. The bed in our room was wonderful, comfortable and plush and the telescope in the room provided us a great view of the harbor, Verrazano, Miss Liberty and the surrounding city. It was a beautiful backdrop for the sunset and the lights of the city. The bathroom was large and the shower was terrific. We didn鈥檛 eat at the onsite restaurant but had a drink in the Rise Bar which offers a great view of the city and seems to be a popular gathering spot for casual drinks and a nosh. Throw in tickets to Jersey Boys and dinner at the Gramercy Tavern and the weekend was a total hit. The only comments we would make is the lack of steam/sauna/swimming pool in a relatively new hotel, we were surprised not to have these amenities at a Ritz Carlton. We鈥檝e read other reviews that note that the d茅cor is a bit tired, I have to agree that the rooms could use a freshing up, but overall the hotel is typical of a Ritz Carlton experience, you leave feeling as though you were well cared for and your needs met with courtesy, a smile and the signature 'My Pleasure'!

<Author>cancercaregiver
<Content>Had a nice stay at the Ritz!! My husband and two children went into NYC for 4 nights in mid-December so my husband could go to a couple doctor's appointment and so we could enjoy the Christmas Decorations and see the city all lit up for the holidays.The hotel did not disappoint. We stayed in a 2 bedroom Suite with a great view of the Statue of Liberty. It was very large and certainly big enough for the four of us. It had a full bathroom as well as a half bathroom which was always a nice feature.Room service was very expensive ($32 for a cheeseburger) but I guess that is to be expected if you are staying at a Ritz in New York City. Rooms were always cleaned nicely and had comfortable beds. The lobby had a warm and cozy feel to it and the staff are ever so friendly. You probably hear 10 hello's before you hit the elevator to go to your room. The concierge was great - I believe Scott was the name of the gentleman who arranged for us to have a limo service and then a car service to go to the Christmas Show and to Gordon Ramsey's restaurant.Overall, the Ritz at Battery Park is a good choice. It is a little far from the main areas, like Central Park, and 57th street, but if you take a taxi or the subway, you can still get there. I would stay here again.

<Author>kmt2008
<Content>Big rooms, fabulous views We stayed at the Ritz Carlton on the night of our wedding. It was wonderful. The rooms are spacious by New York standards. As a New York native, I've been to many other hotel rooms that cost more and are tiny and cramped. I love any opportunity to stay downtown, away from the hordes of tourists you'd certainly find in mid-town. The view of from our room was wonderful. We both slept like babies!We booked the honeymoon special. The room was beautifully arranged. The bathroom and tub are spacious and water was nice and hot. Staff was very nice, but not too in-your-face/annoying as they can be in some upscale joints. We had room service in the morning. It was fast and friendly. And quite tasty. Cabs were plentiful outside of the hotel. Checking out was super fast and we were able to head out fast and easily.

<Author>lilfella
<Content>classy retreat we stayed with our toddler in a harbor view room at the ritz carlton last weekend and felt very well looked after. the welcome - a speedy check-in and chilled champagne for us and an adorable teddy bear for our son - set the tone. we had a standard room which was spacious, well-appointed and in a good state of upkeep - no cracks, chips or 80s furniture hangovers. the bathroom was spacious and so nice to see bulgari white tea toiletries - appropriate brand for an urban luxury hotel. housekeeping were fantastic - a crib was in the room when we arrived made up as requested, and when our son was sick late at night, they silently appeared without fuss, cleared up kiddy vomit from the carpet and crib, moved in a fresh crib and sheets, and left him in peace. we booked a really terrific babysitter upon a recommendation from the hotel - the service was not cheap at $27 per hour plus additions, but for peace of mind, well worth it. my only quibbles, and these were very irritating, were a) that the concierge CONSTANTLY put us on hold whenever we called for help - this is so rude - and b) the bellman who took our luggage down to the lobby hung around for a tip and told us that he probably would not be around when we returned to collect the luggage mid afternoon - yet when we returned at our appointed time, to our surprise there he was. it's disappointing to see service transgressions at such a terrific hotel.

<Author>dannymcl
<Content>At these prices - charging for Internet access is a sheer rip-off! A very nice modern hotel located at the southern tip of Manhattan by Battery Park. Comfortable rooms, top quality (Bulgari) toiletries, lots of staff on duty to hold open doors and generally fuss. In fact with their earpieces and cuff microphones, it did feel like the US Secret Service had taken over the hotel - arguably a bit pretentious. Does it really need two young people to hold open the doors and say hello and goodbye. One feels the room prices just reflect the top-heavy level of staffing. Ironically, when it came to getting my bags out of the baggage room on departure, the whole process came apart at the seams and it took close to 7 minutes to retrieve my luggage! That was funny.My room was towards the back so looked over a flat room and in the distance a building site and Apartments in a modern high rise block where no one seems to have curtains. Interesting goldfish-bowl views of modern New Yorkers' breakfast rituals with aproned nannies tending to toddlers. Do they not realise the hotel guests look into their apartments?My biggest beef about this place was the charge for Internet access. At over $430 per night, you would think they would throw in Internet access for free. If a Knights in in Horseheads, NY can do so for $35 per night, then why can't the Ritz Carlton - that is a sheer rip-off.I was attending a business function there and asked the Concierge to get some flowers for one of the participants. We wanted loud / brash / big / showy - what we got was (a) small and pretentious first time around and (b) slightly bigger and pretentious second time around. To add insult to injury, they never even provided me with a bill from the florist which is really inconvenient for when the time comes to claim expenses.I had dinner there one evening. Although I asked for a well done steak, it came out pretty red in the centre. It's not a hard thing to get correct and that was a let down - I had higher expectations. The restaurant on the ground floor has a dark moody evening restaurant ambience, unfortunately for a hotel which I guess caters for mainly business people, the dark tables remain darkened at breakfast too. An apologetic waiter recognised the problem and I heard him say this to other guests on both days. This is not a place to have breakfast if you want to do some reading in comfortable light. A serious design error.Overall, great rooms, great location, looks good, but let down by the details.

<Author>Nash_Andrew
<Content>Excellent Experience. Stayed one night (5/26) at the Ritz Carlton Battery Park in NYC. We booked the room over the phone on Saturday afternoon and checked in 20 minutes later. Rate was $299.00. Upon arrival we were greeted by three employees in the lobby who poured champagne for us while we checked in. We were upgraded to the Club Floor upon check in. Room was immaculate, save for slightly worn carpet in the entry hall. Overall room was very large, with a huge marble bathroom, separate tub and stand up shower, plush bed linens, etc. View was of the city though we couldn't see too much due to a low floor. Hotel is only about 15 floors high, everything higher is the residences.Service on the club floor was perfect. I asked for more champagne when I walked in and another bottle was out within two minutes. Hors de ouvres were excellent and the wines available were varied and paired well with the food offerings. Service was not at all stuffy but incredibly accomodating. Other than the carpet in the room I previously mentioned, the only other issues were these: a very mediocre, 10-inch pizza from room service was $37.00 -- too much even for the Ritz in NYC. Also, we asked for our room to be tidied up while we went out for the evening... to get rid of the glasses and plates from the club room... and this was not done. Overall we were very pleased other than these minor issues and will return to the Ritz when the occasion arises.

<Author>Insight725
<Content>Loved the Hotel, only complaint is food The Ritz lived up to most of my expectations of a 5-star hotel. Staff were excellent, including check-in, bellman, and concierge, but especially the club level staff. If you can get an Expedia deal, its definitely worth it to stay on the club level. Rooms met expectations, large, well-appointed, bathrooms large, separate shower - no complaints about the room or bathroom, both excellent. Lounge is overpriced and food is not very good and you get only small portions. For the prices they charge, if you're going to serve below average or just average good, the least you can do is provide large portions. Great location if you need to be in the financial district, just a short walk to Battery Park and the Staten Island Ferry. Great food for a lot less at Gigino's, Italian restaurant just across from the Ritz or try Battery Gardens. I would definitely stay here again but only through the Expedia rate, its not worth more than $600 a night for a regular room.

<Content>Super Hotel Experience We stayed only 1 night at the end of our 10-day trip to get away from the people. <Author>Surferdl
<Content>Different Experience We stayed at this property in December 2006 to visit some relatives and take the kids to see the city for the holiday season. We stayed 4 nights.My experience was really different that I expected for a 5 star hotel. I have stayed at other Ritz and Four Season hotels and usally find them really great.The doorman were good, and helpful for getting us a taxi.The spa is small but the massage I got was good and the staff were very nice. Work out room is excellent.1. First we came via limo from LGA which is about a 30 min drive depending on traffic, The hotel limo service was there upon arrival and were great to bring two childrens seats for the limo which was very important to me since I have a 4-year old and a 7 month year old. 2. Doorman, bellservice was quick and had all of our luggage loaded up in a very effecient manner.3. At check in, we were greeted nicely and a small chest filed toy bin, for the little ones. Check-in process was fast and we were up to our room rather quickly. The room had the baby crib that we requested, with two small stuffed bears for the girls. My rate was around $750.00 per night, for a premium room with a view of the statue of lIberty.4. This is where the fun starts, first the room was clearly a room for the handicapped. I am not handicapped, nor is any one in my family, and I believe these rooms should be used for people that really need it. There was no bath tub, which is essential for the babies. The hotel was well aware of that we were coming with our two kids, I was shocked, but I called down to see if we can move to another room, and they told us the premium rooms were totally booked. I asked to be upgraded, and they said for $250.00 more per night we can get a suite. I said fine, and we were quickly moved to a suite with a view of two tall buildings on the other side without the views of the statue of liberty. I wasnt even going to move again.5. The suite was quite large for NYC and i thought is was well apointed. Nice living room, nice master bedroom, wondeful bathroom and closets. I would expect flat screen tvs, but they do not have them, its amazing to me when I travel to Asia, the rooms are so much more advanced. The bathtub was great, especially for my wife and daughters after a long day in the CIty. There is no wireless internet, but DSL for a charge. The location is out of the way for Mid-Town and taxi rides are necessary, but THE LOCATION IS GREAT FOR THE BUSINESS TRAVELER FOR THE FINANCIAL DISTRICT.6. The bar in the lobby is nice with views of the bay and the food was good (appetizers), and the lounge on I think on the 11th, was great for a drink with wonderful views.Concierge I felt was a little off, since I asked them no less that 3 times to get a movie list(DVDS)for the little ones and it never came, but they did recommend quite a few restaraunts to eat at, but never offered to make reservations for us.7. Well upon our day of departure it was 30 degress and windy, our flight was at 5:00pm and I requested to see if we can have a late check out. We were denied. I was stunned since i was paying around 1100 per night (4 Nights) and we had two small children. If it was my wife and I only, it would not have been a big deal, as we would have just cruised around the City for a few hours. The bellman checked our luggage into the storage and we basically had to entertain our kids and keep them warm for 4 hours until we went to the Airport. I decided to fill out the comment card in the room (first time ever for me and Im 33), and let the management know what was going on with us. Im really not that picky, but I felt that this should be known.I was contacted around 6 weeks later by the manager of the hotel, he was very apologetic, and actually offered us a free night next time we come ( I did not ask, nor did I expect it). He also asked why didnt I ask for him upon check-out to get the late check-out. I said why should I have to at a 5-Star hotel. He was very nice, and I really did appreciate the call, when he asked if we would come back, I said probably not and we will stay at the 4 Seasons next time. He was very nice and really did end up sending us a free night via letter.Overall it is a nice hotel great location to the financial district a bit away from Mid-town, just some things happened to us. BTW, it was the same girl when I checked in and put us in the handicapped room, as well as denied our request for late check-out. She was very polite, but Ill let you decide what to think after reading this review.

<Author>ocGlobetraveler
<Content>Impressive by New York Hotel Standards The Ritz-Carlton Battery Park New York offers a contemporary hotel experience, with comforts not so frequently found in most other New York City hotels.Over the years, I have had the opportunity to experience several Manhattan hotels, yet I continue to return to the Ritz-Carlton Battery Park for several reasons. I find that most NYC hotels, even those in the four and five star categories, often lack space. For $300-400 per night, my preference is to at least have a room that is comfortable and spacious. The Ritz-Carlton Battery Park offers spacious accommodations (comparable to those found at other RC properties) but at respectable prices by NYC standards. Although some may argue that the location is somewhat distant I would much prefer comfort and service with a decent price. Other properties with comparable amenities and room sizes (ie . Four Seasons New York, Mandarin-Oriental, Ritz-Carlton Central Park) often charge in excess of $700 per night for comparable accommodations.Battery Park is located at the lowest point in Manhattan, just adjacent to Wall Street and the Statue of Liberty. Although distant from Mid-Town, it's convenient to SoHo, Meatpacking District, Financial District, Chinatown, Chelsea etc. If you're visiting NYC as a tourist, I don't find this property all that inconvenient, as the aforementioned neighborhoods are all at your disposal. Yes, Time Square and Central Park are a cab ride away, but who wants to spend most of their time there anyway?Rooms are consistent with most other Ritz-Carlton properties, particularly those of the more contemporary minded. Bathrooms are some of the most spacious in all of Manhattan, featuring separate glass enclosed showers and individual soaking tubs. The beds are also extremely comfortable, with feathertop beds and high end linens.If you're able to book a room on the club level, I would highly recommend this decision. For an additional $100-150 per night, the Club Level offers you and your guest鈥檚 five daily food presentations from breakfast to evening dessert. Alcoholic beverages are also included (they offer top shelf liquor)For those traveling to NYC on the weekend, this hotel probably offers the best value in the city. Weekend rates begin at $295/night.

There were aspects of the hotel that I liked a lot, but other that I though were disappointing, especially at such a high end hotel.The hotel had great food- some of the best food that I鈥檝e had at a hotel. If you like Mojitos, try them, even if, as to be expected , they are very pricey. The breakfast items at the Nine West restaurant were great, if pretty pricey. Though delicious hash browns and bacon are a bargain at $8, their delicious orange juice was $6 a glass!Service, as to be expected, was very good at the Ritz CarltonThe hotel was very cheerful and the rooms were quite large, especially for New York City.. I prefer a sleek model design, when it comes to d茅cor, and the furnishings at this Ritz Carlton, reminded me of staying with a wealthy older relative with slightly old fashioned tastes.The gym was adequate (it had nice views on the 14th floor). But is did not compare to the gyms I鈥檝e used at the Four Seasons and Park Hyatt hotels. Even some Westins and Hyatts I鈥檝e stayed in have had better hotels. There is also no pool, which is surprising at a high-end hotel such as this.The location of the hotel, way downtown as far as you can go can be seen as a plus or a minus. It is somewhat isolated and is probably quite inconvenient if you want to spend most of you time in midtown. However, we were holding a conference and the isolation worked to our advantage since there were fewer outside distractions. On the plus side, there is also a subway stop, two streets away, and the hotel is next to a beautiful waterfront promenade that is great for strolling and running.One of the things that bothered me most about the hotel is that I was put in a handicapped room (the bathroom did not have a seeperate shower stall like most of the rooms in the hotel). I wish they had told me that and given me the opportunity to wait for another room.I might stay here again for a business event, but overall I don鈥檛 think it is great value for the money.

<Author>drgoofy
<Content>Great Property, Great Stay I just returned from a stay at this property and I had a great time. This was my second stay at Battery Park. I booked directly through the RC website and snagged a great deal. The service was impeccable, and the staff was friendly and welcoming. The room was quite large (I had a king bed with a city view) and very clean. The bathroom was large with great ammenities that were replaced daily. I ordered room service for breakfast and it was on time to the second. I found the food excellent (though pricey). I also had dinner at 2 West and that too was excellent as was the service.The big drawback, as others on this site have mentioned, is the distance from midtown/uptown activities such as the theatres or major museums. It's a pricey cabride, and this depends on the driver (some know shortcuts so pay attention). However, if you're willing to brave the subway, it's a walk across the street, and you're only two stops outside of SoHo and three to four stops outside of Greenich Village (cab rides to SoHo from the hotel are about $7). Still, I like this property best. The view sof the Hudson and Statue of Liberty are breathtaking, and there are lovely littled tucked away restaurants and grocery stores within a couple blocks walking distance. I had dinner at a restaurant called The Cove and not only was it reasonably priced it was absolutely outstanding. If you're a person that has to be in the thick of it, 24 hours a day, this isn't for you. However, if you're the person who wants to do business/play all day and then come to a chic, comfortable, calm room at night, this is the place for you.

<Author>Handsup
<Content>A great experience My wife and I stayed here for a one-night getaway booked through Amex Platinum Travel, which entitled us to a complementary lunch and continental breakfast for 2. We were also upgraded upon arrival from a city view to harbor view room. This is a very clean, straightforward Ritz Carlton. The decor is modern and while the rooms are not lavish (no double sinks and no sitting area) they are very comfortable and the view of the harbor is stunning (probably unmatched by any other NYC hotel). The service throughout our stay was excellent and the staff seem to be very well trained and pleasant. During the stay, my wife also had a massage at the spa and she said it was among the best she has ever had. I used the gym, which was not huge but had a decent array of treadmills/ellipticals and freemotion free weights. I highly recommend the Rise Bar for a quick pre-dinner cocktail. It would be even better in the summer as there is a terrace outside which is set up with additional tables when weather permits.Overall this is not the most lavish Ritz we have ever stayed in, but it was more than adequate, offered excellent service and made for a great break from the stresses of Manhattan. Being in Battery Park City is actually very convenient for going out downtown, and a stroll along the waterfront will leave you with the impression that you're in a different city altogether. We look forward to our next visit!

<Content>Can't Wait to Go Back We had a fabulous one-night stay at the Ritz-Carlton. From the moment we checked in, everything was great. <Author>tymelyron
<Content>go for the view Stayed here for a nearby family function over Saturday night a few weeks ago. We had two rooms, one a harbor view overlooking the Statue of Liberty, the other a city view, which was limited by the other high rise apartments nearby. The harbor view was definitely worth the extra price, which was on par with other hotels of the same caliber, such as the Peninsula and Four Seasons. The rooms were large and refined, not over the top but had a quiet elegance; the beds were most comfortable and the bathroom full of marble. Be sure to check back on the hotel website as the reservation nears, as the price booked a couple of months back actually dropped as our date neared, and the hotel changed the rate. Overnight parking is steep ($60) and the Sunday buffet brunch at the hotel restaurant likewise ($45) though top notch; the hotel is close to the ferry and downtown attractions, but a haul from midtown. Service was helpful, and all in all the stay was most enjoyable.

<Author>MaryStarbucks
<Content>Lovely and Quiet Battery Park Ritz Just checked out of the hotel today - overall I found the hotel to be lovely - the room was very large, great amenities (Bulgari bath products), nice turn-down service at night, comfortable bed, very friendly and helpful staff (see exception below). I'd never stayed in the Battery Park/Financial District area before and was pleasantly surprised by the lack of street noise at night (as compared to hotel stays midtown and in meatpacking district). Paid a similar rate to what I paid at the Hotel Gansevoort recently and got a much larger room with better extras.The only reason I am not giving an Excellent rating was the poor service I received from the doormen (3) upon leaving the hotel. When I walked out with my bags there was one helping another departing party into their car and two others standing around talking with a driver. I made eye contact with one of those two and asked if I could get a cab. He ignored me completely but said something to the doorman who had been helping the other guest who then whistled for a cab. As the cab started to pull up, they continued to ignore me and didn't wave the driver up to where I was (which they could have), so I walked back to the cab and when I couldn't get the door by myself because of my bags, one of the doormen finally walked over and opened the door for me. If they had been very busy, I would have understood, but I was the only one waiting for help at the time and there were three of them. Very dissappointed in this from a common courtesey standpoint, let alone for the rate I paid to stay at the Ritz. It was not a nice way to end my stay, which was otherwise lovely.

<Author>coppellite
<Content>Quiet and Elegant Our family stayed over Labor Day weekend at the Ritz. We caught a play, did some sightseeing and attended the US Open.Staff was very friendly and furnishings nice indeed. We had a city view (looking north) which was just fine. I'm sure the harbor views are even better.We liked the solitude of the location and lack of traffic noise at night(plus the reasonable room rate). Make sure you take in a walk around Battery Park and then head up the nice walkway on the Hudson side to One World Financial. Great landscaping, yachts in port, etc. Then you can enter One World Financial and view Ground Zero from their lobby area. (This is a 4-5 block walk)You can also walk over to the Seaport (which is about 10 blocks from the Ritz). We did this and had some pizza at Pizzeria Uno.Unfortunately the subway stops near Battery Park don't operate on weekends, so you must cab it to go uptown. Other downside is the lack of restaurants within walking distance (although there are a few in the shopping/retail area of One World Financial). Cab rides to midtown are around $15.Did not eat at the hotel except for drinks/appetizers at the lounge bar called Rise on the 14th floor. Very nice with great views on Statue of Liberty, Ellis Island, etc. We even saw the Queen Mary 2 docked off Governors Island.There is a great place one block over called the Amish Market. If you want snacks, drinks, deli items, breakfast just head over there. We ate breakfast there every day for $15 what would have cost $75 with room service.Would definitely stay there again. Also would highly recommend an Italian eatery called Maria Pias in midtown on West 51st. This is just one block west from the Wicked theater. Dined with them twice. Great food and reasonable prices.

<Author>gonj
<Content>A Great Stay My wife and I had a very nice stay at the Ritz. We are from NJ and this was just a little getaway for the weekend. We have done this type of trip a number of times before and have typically booked through American Express.We were given an upgrade to a harbor view room at check in. A nice surprise! The room was large and clean. By large, I mean that it was a very nice size for a room in NYC. I've certainly stayed in larger and much much smaller. I can understand the previously mentioned comparisons to a Marriott, but in NYC this was a very nice-sized room. The telescope was a nice added treat and it worked very well. The bathroom was also very large and immaculate. While we didn't get a chance to utilize the bath butler, it looked pretty cool. One other thing: we loved our mattress and the concierge desk was very helpful in showing us how we could purchase the same. Two very restful nights!My wife and I also enjoyed a massage in the spa, which was very clean, professional and relaxing. The restaurant was very nice and the sunday brunch was pretty spectacular: shrimp, cracked crab, salmon, omelettes, waffles, steak, chicken, and a dessert table to die for.Two things stand out in my mind about the RC-BP. One is the service. I have never been in a hotel where everyone, from the maid to the bellman to the front desk staff, were so hospitable and would go out of their way to acommodate us.Secondly, the location worked out very well for us. We live 5 miles outside of NY and were very happy to be removed from midtown. We spent all our time in Battery Park (the Museum of Jewish Heritage is a great stop) and also walked to Brooklyn (over the Brooklyn Bridge) and to Tribeca and Soho.A beautiful hotel with all the amenities you would expect from 5 stars.

<Author>Gregdu
<Content>Its okay, not up to Ritz Standards Stayed here just 1 night in August 2006. For me, the location is not so great, Battery Park is okay, but its quite far from the things we wanted to do in NYC and necessitated $15 cab rides each way to everything we wanted to do; couldn't take the subway reliably cuz of construction happening all over the place. The hotel is new and big, but the lobby is quite small and noisy and active. Lots of groups staying there, and the volume of noise was more than I've come to expect from a luxury hotel. Staff are friendly and check-in was quick, but there was a refinement that was missing there... I did not like the lobby or lobby bar area at all. The room was average size, and reminded me more of a marriot, albeit a nice marriot. The only things in the room that reminded me that I was in a luxury hotel were the size of the bathroom and the Bulgari bath products (nice touch). I've been lucky to stay at some nice properties, so maybe I'm just spoiled? But this hotel left me wanting for more... The best part was the rate that we got, quite below other luxury properties, even mid-range properties, in NYC. The Four Seasons, in comparison, is larger and quieter and has a sophistication about it that can't be beat...the extra cost is worth it. If you want to stay in Battery Park, this is a fine choice, but if you're going to be spending lots of time in midtown or uptown, I'd stay somewhere else. The travel back and forth isn't worth it.

<Author>ms_travelwhiz
<Content>Refined perfection at the Ritz! We spent a recent weekend at the Ritz Carlton Battery Park and were enchanted by the serene, understated elegance of the lobby decor and our spacious, soothingly decorated room. The furniture and condition of the room were simply perfect. The bathroom was large enough to be a mini-spa and was stocked with deluxe Bulgari amenities. The bathrobes are the most luxurious I have ever seen -- super-plush terry with satin piping on the collar and sleeves. As constant travellers, we have seen the good, bad and ugly and this Ritz property sets new and higher standards for hotel excellence.Perhaps the most outstanding feature was the gracious service, which starts from the moment you alight at the entrance and continues until you -- sadly -- must depart. We enjoyed breakfast in our room and the room service fare was delicious and -- notably -- promptly served.Do try one of the baths on the bath menu. Once selected, the bath butler will transform your bathroom into a candle-lit, aromatherapy event, and serve you a glass of champagne before leaving you to indulge in the perfect bath.We paid only $275/night for this little slice of heaven and will gladly return when we are next in New York.

<Author>Doppelganger69
<Content>Perfect room  I spent a delightful three nights here with my two-year-old son, and had a wonderful time. We had a Harbor View room, and although I couldn't make heads or tails of the telescope, it really wasn't necessary. We delighted in our wonderful views of the Statue of Liberty, Ellis Island, the water taxies and ferries, and so on. Our bathroom was the biggest, best-appointed, and most beautiful I've ever had in New York. The room itself was quite big, and even huge by New York standards. The decor was lovely and in perfect condition, and the featherbed was dreamy. My father and his wife stayed across the hall in a city view room. Their room was identical to ours, except for the view, and was $85 less per night. (I felt the extra cost for the view was worth every penny.)We did not stay on the Club level, and I don't know what value it could add to such an already magnificent hotel, unless one needs to eat five times per day.The room was clean, though not spotless: we found an old bottle cap and a luggage key hiding underneath furniture. The housekeeper the first night ordered up a special teddy bear for my son, and my free overnight shoeshine was well done.We ate breakfast in the hotel each morning. The buffet on weekdays offered a delicious selection at a not-too-outrageous price (I think about $25), especially as they didn't charge me for my son. The Sunday buffet was over the top both in presentation and price (at $50). Every day offered a delicious variety of food of impeccable quality.The Ritz is obviously expensive, but we found a much lower rate ($420) on the hotel's web site than its 800-number quoted us ($595). Manhattan rates in general are quite high right now, and I think our rate represented a very good value for what we enjoyed.One minor item is that the front doors to the hotel are quite heavy and not automated. There is a doorman, but he often was otherwise occupied with getting taxis and so on, and opening the doors while wheeling a stroller was a bit of a challenge.My only significant complaint about the Ritz is that the staff tipped the balance between helpful and obsequious, to the point of making me uncomfortable. All my expressions of thanks were met with the responses of My pleasure, or My absolute pleasure. It got so that I tried not to meet the waiter's eye when he refilled my water glass at breakfast, but I even got the my pleasure when I simply smiled and nodded my gratitude. I enjoy fine hotels and excellent service, but not the servility I encountered here.All in all, we had a wonderful stay here, and would return again with absolute pleasure.

<Author>md_travelerMd
<Content>Disappointed with the Ritz-Carlton I've stayed at very nice hotels before, but this was my first time staying at a Ritz-Carlton. Overall, I'd have to say I was somewhat disappointed with the experience as it fell beneath my expectations. First, the positive - the bathroom was VERY nicely appointed and spacious with a bath, shower stall, toilet alcove and large vanity area. Outside of that, the room itself was really nothing more than a standard Marriott room. The service was spotty - when we first arrived (at 3pm) the remnants of another guests' room service was outside of our room (and wasn't taken away for approximately 2 hours). The cleaning lady came into our room prior to checkout to start cleaning. Calls to the concierge, front desk, etc... resulted in unacceptably long wait times. The bathtub stopper wasn't working (although a maintenance worker was quick to come up and fix it). The furnishings were a bit worn (stains on the carpet and gouges in some of the wood furniture). When the valet brought our car around at checkout, he did not even offer to help load bags into the car.At a hotel that does not carry the Ritz-Carlton brand (or pricing) I would have written all this off as minor nuisances; at the Ritz, I expected better.

<Author>brig70
<Content>Great Service and consistent with other properties I live in NY but will stay at NYC hotels when celebrating certain occasions with my wife. We celebrated Valentine's Day and spent a night at this hotel. I selected one of the packages they were offering for that weekend. I almost selected the helicopter ride package but felt the couples massage would be a better value. I'm glad I did.Overall appearance: The property is very clean and there were a lot of business people around. It's a few blocks away from Wall Street, so it seemed that this is one of the places to meet for a off site meeting or an after-work place to meet for drinks. The hotel is a bit difficult to find unless you (or your cab driver) is familar with Battery Park.Room: Very surprised with the size. I was quite happy with it. It wasn't as small as I anticipated and had a very nice sized bathroom. The shower had a good flow for being on a higher floor and very powerful. (I know a few people that would find that point helpful..) Rooms were clean and a comfortable bed. I had a harborview room and it also came with a telescope to check out the Statue of Liberty. You can save up to $100 bucks to get a city view room which I would have done had it not been part of the package. Besides, do you spend most of your stay looking out your window?Massage:The massages that were part of the package were EXTREMELY relaxing. The two women who gave us massages were very professional and knew what they were doing. My wife and I agreed that it was well worth it. The spa is located on the harbor side, so unless a firetruck comes blaring down the West Side Highway, you really can't hear the city noise that much. Plus, they had music playing at a comfortable level. In a few short minutes, you end up relaxing and ready for the massage.Before we went out to dinner, we grabbed a few drinks at the top floor bar. Great views and the clientel were young professionals. You'll pay premium prices since it's the Ritz, but the bartender made great martini's and gimlets. We returned that evening for our Valentine's Day Chocolate Bar dessert. The staff was nice enough to accomodate us an hour earlier than our original reservation time. The Chocolate Bar was in a private room with about 10 other couples. Think Salad Bar but with desserts. Not monstrous slices of cake or mousse, but small dishes that really wet your appetite. There were a ton of selections to choose from and capped off the evening wonderfully. Overall, I was very pleased with this hotel. Consistent with other Ritz Carlton's and would recommend it to others. If you are on a business trip to Lower Manhattan (and your per diem allows it) I would select this hotel. Normal rooms go for $300 and up. So, if you are a stickler like I am when it comes to rooms, you can't go wrong here.

<Author>adamunc
<Content>Terrific Hotel, Inconvenient Location Stayed at the R-C Battery Park for a couple of days as a tourist due to fantastic AAA rates [$265/night]. The hotel itself is a dream--very modern style, unlike the Mediterranean or English Country style of most of this chain. The lobby is minimalist but unquestionably high quality. Staff was, as always, smooth and polished. It always seemed like they were waiting for us to arrive with a request. The rooms are, of course, quite nice. We were given a corner unit [without requesting], so we had two windows and lots of light, with expansive views. Had a peek into some non-corner rooms and there is considerably more space in the sitting area of a corner room, plus an entry hallway, so ask for one if you'd like the extra square footage. Decor is very Laura Ashley, with pastel soft greens and yellows. Some slight faded stains on the carpet. Bathroom was marble and large, with the signaure Ritz bath menu and great water pressure. Beds are dangerously comfortable and quite plush, as you would expect. The 14th-floor lounge, Rise, was smaller than I expected on the interior but still quite nice with reasonably-priced drinks and small meals. The outdoor terrace was not open due to chilly temperatures, but it was certainly a memorable hotel lounge.Now... the location. If you had business in Lower Manhattan or wanted to limit your tourism to Wall St., Statue of Liberty, Staten Island Ferry, Ground Zero, Chinatown... it would be fine. There is construction going on all around the hotel, with roads diverted every which way. Truly confusing, and it takes a bit of doing to get to a subway stop. It's not a terribly long walk, but it is circuitous. Getting back and forth to Midtown/Theatre District, etc. can be a nightmare--especially, as when I was there, if they shut down the subway in the evenings due to the construction. Plan on $15-$25 cab ride to Midtown, and a bit of a wait with the valets to hail a cab, as they don't come by the hotel as frequently as they do at Midtown hotels.Staten Island Ferry is terrific and free; views of the Statue from the hotel are great; food is somewhat limited in the hotel's immediate vicinity.

<Content>Fantastic weekend at the Ritz! Wow! Just returned from a fantastic weekend at the Ritz Battery park. We have stayed at many Ritz Carlton hotels and this one rates right up at the top. <Content>Lovely hotel, away from it all but in the city My (now) fiancee and I are New Yorkers, and spent the night after getting engaged at the Ritz Battery Park. It was truly a lovely experience. The hotel is kind of isolated at the very Southern tip of Manhattan - if you're looking to be in Manhattan but away from the hustle and bustle, that's great. If you're visiting the City, and want to be _in_ the hustle and bustle, it wouldn't be so great. That being said, it was perfect for us.

<Author>AnnieKingston_NY
<Content>Downtown Ritz--My Home-from-Home Let's get the negatie out of the way at once: yes, it is surrounded by building sites, and also by the greatest water view on Manhattan Island. Yes, if you hate building sites it is not the place to be. And yes, if you want to stroll the boulevards and window-shop, you'll have to walk a few blocks through buiding sites first.Now to the good: If you want to stay in a 5-star hotel in Manhattn and you want to spend less than $600 pr night, this is the place to go. In fact, if you want to spend less than $300 pr night...which makes it lower-priced than many 3- and 4-star hotels in Manhattan--then this is the place to go. For first-time travelers to NYC or people with large families, this will be inconvenient; you'll want to spend more for a comfortable hotel nearer the heart of town. But for true New Yorkers, this is one of the last of the great bargains. Everything you'd expect from a 5-star hotel, including excellent food and a big 400 sq ft room, not to mention immense bathroom. Beds to beat the most Heavenly in town. Caring, personal service (I visit here with my 16-yr-old who is developmentally disabled, and they are always very friendly and caring and responsive). It's all there and it's all wonderful.

<Author>shipwreckedcanuk
<Content>True hotel luxury We enjoy coming to NYC for 2-3 day getaways on weekends. Despite what many people feel, we almost always stay in the Financial area during these trips (We loved the now closed Regent Wall Street). On the weekends they have great rates and the hotels are much less crowded. We only take one cab out and one cab back a day- $40. If you compare that to the price difference between staying downtown on a weekend or central park, its cheap! We stayed in a Club floor, water facing room for $445/night. The Club floor has the usual lounge with free food and drinks a few times a day. What was different was the quality of the food and drink. It didn't feel like 'free' stuff- everything they served for free would have fit in perfectly had it been served in the downstairs restaurant. Two special notes, the cheese board they served had cheese from Artisanal (a fantastic NYC cheese shop/bistro) and they served champagne, not sparkling wine- both suprise treats for club lounge freebees.The room itself was large and had a fantastic view of Battery Park and the Statue of Liberty. The telescope looked good in the room, but was a piece of junk- a nice pair of binoculars would have been a better idea. The bed was great and they got our bedding request just right (you can order different kinds of pillows and mattress tops). The bathroom was spacious and well stocked. It was just what you'd expect from an upmarket chain hotel- not personal, but in excellent taste. The staff was perfect. They did the standard remember your name thing and what you drink, but they did it without it seeming strained. When they called us by name it was always correct and if they were unsure, they just used 'sir' or 'ma'am'. They were just professionals doing an excellent job.My only concern is with the car serive. We arranged through the hotel to be picked up and dropped of at JFK. For $150+tip (each way!) you'd expect something more than a generic black sedan car service. I mentioned this to the concierge and was told that it was a competitive rate.... Ah well, they were on time, polite, and the cars were clean.

<Author>jackosan
<Content>Quiet Downtown Luxury This luxury hotel lies at the far southern tip of Manhattan and is mainly for business travelers. The building is new, the rooms are elegantly appointed and decently-sized and the public areas are very attractive. In the right room, the views of New York Harbor are stunning.This is the third or fourth time that I have stayed here and I have never had a bad experience. The work-out facilities are quite nice and the restaurant is up-scale hotel fare. It is far and away the nicest hotel available in lower Manhattan. Battery Park City itself is a quite oasis of largely residential tranquility. Strolling along the water, you might forget you are in Manhattan. While the staff can seem a bit obsequious (a Ritz hallmark), they are quite competent and helpful, and generally better than the union-job-for-life attitude of most mid-town hotel employees.Now, to address a few gripes from previous Tripadvisor reviews: First, if you want to be in mid-town, by all means stay in mid-town instead of grousing about how far away this hotel is (not that it's all that difficult to walk a couple of blocks and catch an express train uptown for two measely bucks.) Second, if you want a cheap breakfast (or any other meal), you're not going to find it in an upscale Manhattan hotel.Bottom line, if I need to be downtown, the Ritz is the place for me.  
<Date>Dec 12, 2005

<Author>yawn
<Content>Nice Hotel Stayed at this hotel for 3 nights. rooms were well equipped and spacious for New York. stayed on the 11th floor on the club level so had the benefits of a morning buffet breakfast and early evening presentations which included both complementary wine and champagne or soft drinks if your tee total!. staff were both helpful and courteous at all times top marks to max who served at the club level and also the concierge who arranged a limo back to the airport for us. the views from the rise bar out on the balcony was great at night{if a little chilly at this time of year} although drinks were a little pricey at over $8 for a bottle of beer once tax is added.The only disappointment was the food at the ground floor Restaurant. <Author>qaz123
<Content>Great Hotel; Out-of-the-Way Location This is an excellent hotel, with attentive service, in an out-of-the-way location. Upside: The rooms are large and nicely appointed. The bathrooms are huge and luxurious. And the common areas are new, clean, and lavish. The fitness center is fantastic--a well-equipped room on the 14th floor overlooking the harbor. Even the food is pretty good, if a bit expensive.Downsides: The location, location, location. Though it is near a number of subway lines, there is much construction in the area, making it difficult to reach these lines. More importantly, should you not want to take the subway, cabs to any part of the city are very expensive and construction sometimes snarls traffic. Fares range from $20 or so to midtown to $10 to Tribeca. Expect to spend some real money on taxis if that is the way you prefer to get around. Or just get on an expense account.Bottom Line: If you can stomach the cab fares and don't mind having to travel rather considerable distances anytime you want to eat outside the hotel, then you can't go wrong with this hotel.
