<Author>GlobalQueen
<Content>Not Impressed - Spotty Service My husband and I stayed here for my birthday August 12-14th. We have stayed at the hotel three weekends over the past month. We had better visits the previous weekends, thus we chose to stay again this time hoping for a good experience over this special weekend. We were wrong.Initially, we were excited that perhaps the concierge was planning a small surprise (ie. upgrade or complimentary dessert) as they called to confirm the reservation, know the exact time of our arrival and acknowledged the Birthday. They had a lovely bottle of champagne on ice for my husband one of the previous trips we were there.No one was there to greet up upon arriving at the hotel and we carried in our own luggage until a bellman saw us coming into the hotel where they intercepted our luggage. We were checked in by Ann (a pleasant reception clerk) who remembered my name from previous trips. She told my husband that she would do something special for the occasion. We were given a low floor city view that looked over a pile of construction. Across the room from ours was a plate of raw salmon and a shrimp cocktail that had been partially eaten. The hallway smelled.After we returned from dinner later that evening, the food was still in the hallway and a bag of garbage next to another room was sitting outside of it. We noticed the drain in our room was clogged so we decided to report it the next morning.After we returned to the hotel at 4pm the next day, the clog in the drain had not been fixed, no special amenity had been delivered, the garbage bag from the morning was still in front of the other guests room and our room had not been cleaned! We called down asking if the room could be cleaned and drain fixed. My husband also inquired separately and a gentleman at guest reception assured us it would be fixed with an additional special amenity. On our way to dinner, the gentleman was in our elevator and confirmed our hotel room number publicly (he must have remembered my husband and there was a to do item on his list. After we returned from dinner that night, there was a plate of chocolate covered strawberries in our room. Unfortunately, we could not eat them, as they were warm and we had just had dinner and dessert, but at least the room had been cleaned (albeit haphazardly and hastily), but not the drain. We figured since we were checking out in the morning, we would refrain from commenting on our problems yet again!Overall, I might stay at the hotel again (but only if the price was very, very competitive), but not for the service from the majority of the hotel staff. I would think that at a four or five star property, that something as simple as unclogging the drain would have to go through multiple requests. The only bright light during the stay came from Kamlyn in the Rise Bar. She has a very infectious laugh, a great demeanor and is attentive and mingles with her guests. Perhaps this disappointing stay was an anomaly, but I will likely stay at other true 5 star properties next time in NY.

<Author>Nyquist
<Content>Great Hardware, Bad Software I paid $359 for a harbor view room, bfast and parking included. This is a special weekend rate and you cannot do better in NYC for this price. I give the hotel five stars across the board at this price point.However, this is the Ritz, and most people travelling during the week will pay much more, and the hotel falls short of the prices they normally demand.The Good:- Rooms are large, mine was spotless, and quality was excellent. Housekeeping was outstanding.- Service throughout the hotel is attentive, almost overbearing. I was with my family and they made us feel welcome, even with a cranky two year old.- Location is really great, soho and tribeca are close at hand.- Property is new, high quality, and very upscale. Piano bar at night is great.The Bad:- Went down for breakfast on Sunday morning and the buffet was being set up for a 9AM start. It was clear that most of the kitchen resources were deployed on this effort. We ordered from menus at 8:35 and didn't get our food until 9AM... should have just waited.- Wife was down in bar Sat night. I was in room with aforementioned two year old and 4 month old. Needed mommy ASAP... phone call to downstairs bar indicated no one was there... my wife was there the whole time (at least that is what she told me)The Ugly:- Checked in, standard Ritz big-to-do procedures, but in the chaos I forgot to notice they didn't return my license and credit card. I figured it out once we got to the room. I figured it out in the room while the bell hop unloaded our gear- he was on the problem immediately and I got an apology from the front desk via phone. Still- this should not happen.- Got charged $100 for parking though it should have been included. Didn't notice when I checked out. I called back a few days later and it was resolved.In short, a great property, particulalry if you don't care about being in MidTown (SoHo and Tribeca are Walkable). I prefer this location to midtown. The weekend deal is unbeatable. If you are expecting true 5-star and are paying 5-star prices, you may be dissapointed.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel a little out of the way This is a good hotel. I disagree with a previous review that ripped the hotel. For someone who claims to know NYC, the review didn't show it. The rooms are average NYC size which are generally small. But the appointments are very nice, the staff knowledgeable and helpful and the location tolerable unless you are spending your entire time in midtown. Contrary to what was earlier written, cabs do line up. I had no problem getting a taxi. There is construction going on next door. And the road around Battery Park is a mess. You will experience noise during the weekdays and on Saturday from about 9-5 in the city view rooms. I am very sensitive to hotel noise. But considering the construction ends before evening, it isn't too bad. However, to balance out the location and the construction you need to get a room for under $350. Over that, I would look somewhere else. Especially if you are going to midtown most days. I have found Ritz Carltons and Four Seasons somewhat stiff in terms of decor etc. And you can expect the services and restaurants to be pricey, but the overall experience is fine. One recommendation to management, designate one or two floors as quiet areas. Prohibit people who insist on bringing offspring from staying on or visiting those floors. I have the feeling that most peole who bring children to this category hotel are just looking to tell anyone who will listen that they stayed at the RizCarlton with their legitimate or otherwise kids. Keep them away from me.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overpriced  My wife and I stayed with our 2 children for a business  pleasure trip. We have traveled to many places throughout the world as a family unit and consider ourselves well-versed in the art of hotel critiquing. Additionally, as I am originally from NY, I have a good sense of the local NY hospitality market.The Ritz Carlton Battery Park is new enough but lacks character and general warmth. Some of this is attributed to the far away location and rather plain service, but much can also be attributed to the small, low, and sterile rooms (despite the over-hyped view of the harbor and Lady Liberty).We found the prices to be quite high for the room, basic services, and food  beverage (which was decent, but not worth 100 USD+ for lunch). We also got the feeling that kids were not welcome (or at least viewed only as a source of more revenue).Additionally, watching the bellmen whistle at cabs half a mile a way was quite entertaining. The hotel cannot line up cabs. One night, it took 40 minutes just to get out of the lobby and on to dinner.Overall, the hotel is about as good as the average Marriott, but then again we weren't paying to receive Marriott-level accommodations and service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice place to stay if you're not adverse to cabs We just returned from a weekend at the Ritz. We were able to check in early and given a complimentary upgrade to a harbor view room which were nice touches. We were also sent chocolates in honor of our anniversary. Since most of our time was spent in Soho and Tribeca, the cab rides were necessary, but reasonable ($8 or so per trip). However, Midtown is easily $20 no matter what time of day you head there between traffic and the distance. The concierge desk was helpful and friendly. Rise bar had a nice terrace facing the Statute of Liberty, good drinks and decent appetizers. It was expensive, though, over $100 for a few drinks and an appetizer platter for two. If you plan to do Midtown or theaters, you are adding at least $50 per day in cabs to your tab. If you are looking to see the tourist attractions in the harbor area or go to Ellis Island, this is an excellent base.

<Author>BaronNorthLincs
<Content>Excellent We stayed here mid February during a four day break to the big apple. The hotel is situated in lower manhattan, near ground zero  overlooks the statue of liberty adjeacent to Hudson bay. The hotel is immaculate, very accomodating and the door staff and porters do everything for you. Our room was very spacious and well equipped with satellite TV, Nintendo mini disc etc. Be aware though, its not cheap to use the facilities or phone home from here. We made a big mistake and they charge almost $30 for connecting a call to the UK, this left us with a bill on check-out of nearly $750. If you plan to eat breakfast in your room I'd advise you only do it the once as it costs in the region of $85 for two. If you can book this hotel and flights via Expedia as we did you can catch a bargin in the region of 拢850 per couple including return flights with Virgin Atlantic, which considering this is a 5 star hotel it's excellent value for money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall Very Nice Experience I stayed at the Ritz-Carlton Battery Park for two nights in early April, and overall found it positive. When I first checked in (on a government rate) I was supposed to be in one of the back side rooms facing the west side highway, but the nice girl at the desk, Donette, upgraded me to a harbor view room on the 6th floor. As others have noted here, the view is really lovely, and yes, there are telescopes in these rooms to better see lady liberty, etc, with. I did not eat at the hotel restaurant as all Ritz-Carlton restuarants are pretty steep, but there is a nice Amish market a few blocks away and behind that a decent expresso place, both reasonable. If you want to stay in the Battery Park area, then this is the hotel for that. Three different subway lines are all within walking distance, and it's fairly straightfoward to get to midtown Manhattan and elsewhere. That said, its a bit of a trek if you want to spend most of your time in the 42nd/Broadway area or at the more upscale restaurants on the Upper East and West sides. The plus is that Chinatown, Village, Soho are not too far away and lower Manhattan has some sweet designer bargain outlets: Century 21 and Syms are within walking distance. Also Wall Street for sightseeing and acces to the Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island ferries. The hotel itself is newish, clean, and mostly quiet, although some noise from the Brooklyn tunnel access is unavoidable, and rooms have big bathrooms with soaking tubs and separate shower, and beds are overstuffed with down padding and duvets, quite comfy. I would recommend this hotel for a romantic getaway or a short business trip.

<Author>1kauai
<Content>Great stay at the Ritz My wife and I stayed at the Ritz Battery Park on 3-11 thru 3-13. I was able to check in at 10:00am. Which was great, since I had flown all night. The staff was very professional and courteous. The Harbor View room was unbelievable. It is worth the extra money, in order to have Ellis Island and the Statue of Liberty in view while you sip coffee or tea from your room. The hotel is located in Lower Manhatten and close to Battery Park and Wall Street. However, to reach Midtown or Uptown you need to take a taxi ($15.00 to $20.00 one way) or the subway. The Bowling Green subway (4,5) station is within a couple of blocks and can take you within a general proximtiy of any destination Midtown or Uptown. The Rise Bar at the hotels 14th floor is nice for Martini's and the view is unmatched. Did not try any of the food at the hotel restaurant. I would recommend Uncle Jack's Steahouse (Midtown on 9th Ave-$12.00 cab) for dinner but expensive. The area around the hotel feels very safe, since there are Park Police around at all times. The Ritz met and exceeded all of our expectations....Great stay and will return when it is not cold and snowy.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Would stay again... My husband and I stayed here February 18-21, 2005. We wanted to stay downtown for a change and chose the Ritz as part of a package through Expedia. I was slightly worried after reading some of the negative reviews on this website, however, we were pleasantly surprised. We phoned the hotel ahead of time requesting an early check-in since our flight was arriving at 0900. We weren't guaranteed an early check-in but were assured that if this was not possible we could at least leave our luggage at the hotel while we killed some time. Turns out they were able to give us an early check-in which was great. My husband mentioned we were in town for our anniversary and we received a complimentary truffle tray our first night. I have been accused of being overly harsh when critiquing hotels and I really don't have anything bad to say about our stay. We felt it was clean, comfortable, safe, and with the view of Lady Liberty oh so romantic. We can't speak on the quality of the restaurants since we did not eat at the hotel, but the room service pricing was a bit steep. We did not make it to the Rise bar but I'm sure the view is spectacular. For anyone planning a stay in February, inquire about the Chocolate Bar, seems decadent. The only reason we MIGHT not stay again...location. It is relatively far from the action in midtown. If the hotel offered a shuttle we would stay here everytime, no question. Lastly, check-out the Amish market across the street...great for a quick snack or breakfast.

<Author>TMM
<Content>Superb Stay Many advised it would be a bad choice to move hotels (we stayed at the Sofitel also), but we did it anyway and spent our last night here. The outside of the Ritz-Carlton, Battery Park is not impressive once you find out rooms only go to the 14th floor and the rest are of the building is condos. However, once inside the hotel is another story. The reception area is small but lovely. We were whisked to our harbour view room on the 4th floor (again this does don鈥檛 sound impressive) by our personal butler. The room was huge and gorgeous. We had a direct view of the Statue of Liberty and though my husband thought the telescope was on the cheap side it didn鈥檛 stop him from using it. The bed was so comfortable and the amenities were nice. We ordered room service for our son (pizza, French fries and milk) that was very expensive ($38) and again we needed a bottle of milk which they charged us $10 for (ouch!). We have stayed at several Four Seasons with him and we have never been charged for a bottle of milk. The hotel bills itself as very child friendly, but there was little sign of this. Twice we asked for the highly touted children鈥檚 menu and no one seemed to be aware of this. Besides this we found the service to be a bit contrived and overdone. This was shown when two different staff members called my husband by the wrong surname. First he was Mr. Patel and the Mr. Albertson. Apparently, their guest list cheat sheets were wrong. I have never felt the service at the Four Seasons was over the top. The location of the hotel was perfect for the activities we had planned for our last day. We easily walked to Castle Clinton to get our tickets for the Statue of Liberty. After our visit to the Statue and Ellis Island we walked over to Ground Zero to pay our respects and it all became too much for me. I was in NYC for the US Open in 2001 and flew home on 9/10. I applaud those who worked in the area prior to 9/11 continue to do so. It must be hard to walk past the site everyday.

<Author>JamieKate
<Content>Indifferent Friendly check-in, large, well-decorated room, spacious bathroom, comfortable bed, good room service, adequate gym.Was there for a business trip and it served it's purpose - near Wall St, comfortable  clean. If you are going as a tourist I think the location is pretty good - near Statue or Liberty, Ellis Island, subway to uptown from Bowling Green. It's not that nice at nightime - very deserted and nothing open, also can be hard to get a cab from. Great deli - Amish Market - across the street if you don't want to pay usual extortionate room service prices.I wouldn't pick it as a hotel for a special occasion though as it lacks character and charm. As far as business hotels go it's fine, but I can't say I'd rush to go back over anywhere else because just as there is nothing bad about it, there is nothing outstanding about it either. If you have to stay downtown and are just looking for a place to sleep then the Millenium Hilton is better value for money. If you want special then spend your $300 a night somewhere else.

<Author>RJB
<Content>Very nice! Let me add to the positive comments. We stayed four nights in a Harbour View room in October 2004. The room was a good size and, even though only on the fourth floor, had an excellent view. <Author>jujub34ns
<Content>Lovely, but too far from everything else Stayed there earlier this month for a business trip. It's a lovely hotel. The harbor view alone almost makes it worth staying there.I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone who has meetings in the Wall Street area, and whose bill is being paid by a corporate expense account. This hotel won't work for families on vacation or tourists, especially given the distance to any of the major attractions in NYC. The hotel is far from everything except the Financial District. If you plan to do any shopping or dining outside of the area, realize that it's a $15 taxi ride to anywhere in midtown - one way. Even getting around Lower Manhattan was dicey because the cabbies weren't always familiar with the Byzantine layout of the streets. You can certainly try the subway, but the station is several blocks away and the streets are not in a grid pattern (easy to get lost). The walk back to the hotel late at night can be scary.Try to get a higher floor to avoid noise from the street. The hotel part of the Ritz Carlton only goes to the 14th floor. The remainder of the tower is residential and has a separate entrance. The hotel has great windows, but the hotel sits directly above the exit ramp for the Battery Tunnel and the West Side Highway. It's noisy.

<Author>deanmac
<Content>Good hotel. Decent location, but 5 stars? We arrived on May 28th and checked into our standard room, booked though expedia with of their special rates. We *didn't* get the FAO Schwarz bear as part of the Ritz-Kids club, as our booking didn't qualify for this. No-one told us this when we booked. No big deal really, but it's something you may wish to bear in mind (no pun intended) when opting for a cheap rate, especially if you've already told the kids they're getting one!After opening the curtains in our 4th floor room we were greeted by some very nice road maintenance works. Noisy during the day, but no complaints in the evening. My advice would be to ask for a room as high up as possible, but that's good advice for anywhere in Manhattan, but just here :-)Seeing all the reviews posted about this hotel regarding upgraded rooms, I thought I'd give it a try. No joy. I phoned reception to ask about a room upgrade. I was on hold for 10 minutes before giving up. Not very professional. The 2nd time I called, the girl on reception told me that they didn't have any available at the time, but not to worry, she would get back to me and let me know. Needless to say, she never did. Not that I expected her to.I'm not sure why everyone is raving so wildly about this hotel. I've stayed in a few 5 star hotels over the years, and this one isn't anything spectacular. Personally, I'd give it 4 stars, not 5. This isn't really for any negative issues or problems with the hotel, because there really isn't anything wrong with it. It's just that it really isn't that special...

<Content>In a word....SUPERB! We stayed at the Ritz from 02-27 to 02-29 and truly enjoyed our stay. We were upgraded to a waterfront room (w/o asking) and it was lovely! Lauren at the reception desk was so polite and warm, it was refreshing. The entire staff, from the bellman to housekeeping were warm and welcoming, not pretentious! We dined at the 2 West restaurant (onsite) and it was delicious and well priced. I contacted housekeeping for slippers and they were brought to my room within 5 minutes. The maid did a great job cleaning our room each day. Taxi's midtown ranged from 10-14(each way) not including the tip. It was well worth it because the location of this property is lovely. It is quiet and has an understated elegance. Venice Lacy and Chooi Li Loo provided us with a pleasant surprise upon our return to our room the first night. Chocolate covered strawberries (decorated like tuxedos)were placed in our room in honor of our anniversary! What a nice touch! It made our 10th aniversary one to remember. We'll be back!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>too far out we've just returned from a stay at the Ritz, battery park. The hotel was small and very quiet. The room was blandly decorated and we had to pay extra for a harbour view which wasn't really worth it because the statue of liberty is only just in view. The location is awful - you have to get a taxi just about everywhere. The hotel is very expensive - breakfast for 1 adult  2 children came to about $96 and was not that great. I think this hotel is great for business travellers who want to stay downtown but not for families visiting NY.

<Author>Homergirl
<Content>nice, only a few minor complaints My sister and I stayed here only for one quick night after a concert at Madison Square Garden. We weren't able to take advantage of all that the Ritz offered. However upon checking in, the staff upgraded us to a waterfront room and were so pleasant to deal with. We went to the bar on the 14th(?) floor for dessert and tea at 12:00am and although they were done serving food, they were nice enough to get us our chocolate fondue we were craving. The only complaint was that housekeeping did not clean out the minibar from the previous guests, who left their food and drink in it (gross) and there was a very large stain on the carpet next to the window. Other than that, the hotel was beautiful, staff was up to par with Ritz standards, and the rooms and bed were quiet and pleasant. I would highly suggest paying the extra cab fare downtown to this hotel, where it is a bit quieter.
